{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01SaVTJQzXGe4c4LzevctoWZ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"All test cases have explicit `defaults.custom`. Now let me think about what the actual issue is. \n\nLooking at the code again more carefully:\n\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // If custom doesn't exist as a map, skip to next panel\n}\n\n// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions\nif displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n    ...\n}\n\n// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // This is ONLY called if custom exists\n```\n\nThe issue is that `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` is inside the block that requires `custom` to be a map. If `defaults.custom` doesn't exist, the entire panel processing is skipped, including the override migration.\n\nSo the scenario is:\n1. Dashboard saved in v10.3 with table panel\n2. The panel has field overrides with `custom.displayMode`\n3. But the panel does NOT have explicit `defaults.custom`\n4. When v38 migration runs, it skips the panel because `defaults.custom` is missing\n5. The field overrides are never migrated from `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions`\n\nNow the question is: when would a dashboard NOT have explicit `defaults.custom`? \n\nLooking at the code flow, this could happen if:\n1. The dashboard was created before the fieldConfig.defaults.custom concept was introduced\n2. Or the user never explicitly set defaults.custom in the UI\n3. Conversion Flow: v0 → v1 → v2\n    38→\n    39→```\n    40→v0alpha1 (Legacy JSON) → v1beta1 (Migrated JSON) → v2alpha1/v2beta1 (Structured)\n    41→```\n    42→\n    43→#### v0 to v1 Conversion:\n    44→- All schema migrations (v0-v42) are executed in the backend\n    45→- Ports the logic from DashboardMigrator and implements built-in plugin migrations for panel plugins since backend cannot load plugins\n    46→- Transforms legacy JSON dashboards to migrated JSON format\n    47→- Handles backward compatibility for older dashboard formats\n    48→- See [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md) for detailed instructions on creating new schema migrations\n    49→\n    50→#### v1 to v2 Conversion:\n    51→- API version conversions between different Kubernetes API versions\n    52→- Transforms JSON dashboards to structured dashboard format\n    53→- v2 schema is the stable, typed schema with proper type definitions\n    54→- Handles modern dashboard features and Kubernetes-native storage\n    55→\n    56→## Conversion Matrix\n    57→\n    58→The system supports conversions between all dashboard API versions:\n    59→\n    60→| From ↓ / To → | v0alpha1 | v1beta1 | v2alpha1 | v2beta1 |\n    61→|---------------|----------|---------|----------|---------|\n    62→| **v0alpha1**  | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n    63→| **v1beta1**   | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n    64→| **v2alpha1**  | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n    65→| **v2beta1**   | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n    66→\n    67→Each conversion path is automatically instrumented with metrics and logging.\n    68→\n    69→## API Versions\n    70→\n    71→The supported dashboard API versions are:\n    72→\n    73→- For schema version migration implementation details, see the [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md).\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n- [Overview](#overview)\n  - [Conversion Flow](#conversion-flow-v0--v1--v2)\n  - [v0 to v1 Conversion](#v0-to-v1-conversion)\n  - [v1 to v2 Conversion](#v1-to-v2-conversion)\n- [Conversion Matrix](#conversion-matrix)\n- [API Documentation](#related-documentation)\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Grafana dashboard migration system operates across three main conversion layers:\n\n### Conversion Flow: v0 → v1 → v2\n\n```\nv0alpha1 (Legacy JSON) → v1beta1 (Migrated JSON) → v2alpha1/v2beta1 (Structured)\n```\n\n#### v0 to v1 Conversion:\n- All schema migrations (v0-v42) are executed in the backend\n- Ports the logic from DashboardMigrator and implements built-in plugin migrations for panel plugins since backend cannot load plugins\n- Transforms legacy JSON dashboards to migrated JSON format\n- Handles backward compatibility for older dashboard formats\n- See [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md) for detailed instructions on creating new schema migrations\n\n#### v1 to v2 Conversion:\n- API version conversions between different Kubernetes API versions\n- Transforms JSON dashboards to structured dashboard format\n- v2 schema is the stable, typed schema with proper type definitions\n- Handles modern dashboard features and Kubernetes-native storage\n\n## Conversion Matrix\n\nThe system supports conversions between all dashboard API versions:\n\n| From ↓ / To → | v0alpha1 | v1beta1 | v2alpha1 | v2beta1 |\n|---------------|----------|---------|----------|---------|\n| **v0alpha1**  | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n| **v1beta1**   | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n| **v2alpha1**  | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n| **v2beta1**   | ✓        | ✓       | ✓        | ✓       |\n\nEach conversion path is automatically instrumented with metrics and logging.\n\n## API Versions\n\nThe supported dashboard API versions are:\n\n- `dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1` - Legacy JSON dashboard format\n- `dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1` - Migrated JSON dashboard format  \n- `dashboard.grafana.app/v2alpha1` - New structured dashboard format\n- `dashboard.grafana.app/v2beta1` - Enhanced structured dashboard format\n\n## Schema Versions\n\nSchema versions (v13-v42) apply only to v0alpha1 and v1beta1 dashboards:\n\n- **Minimum supported version**: v13\n- **Latest version**: v42  \n- **Migration path**: Sequential (v13→v14→v15...→v42)\n\nFor detailed information about creating schema version migrations, see the [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md).\n\n## Testing\n\nThe implementation includes comprehensive test coverage for conversion-level operations:\n\n- **Backend conversion tests**: API version conversions with metrics validation\n- **Frontend tests**: TypeScript conversion tests  \n- **Integration tests**: End-to-end conversion validation\n- **Metrics tests**: Prometheus counter validation\n\n### Backend conversion tests\n\nThe backend conversion tests validate API version conversions and metrics instrumentation:\n\n- **API conversion tests**: Test conversions between v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, v2beta1\n- **Metrics validation**: Tests verify that conversion metrics are properly recorded\n- **Error handling**: Tests validate error classification and logging\n- **Performance**: Tests ensure conversion operations are efficient\n\n**Test execution:**\n```bash\n# All backend conversion tests\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/... -v\n\n# Metrics validation tests\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestSchemaMigrationMetrics\n```\n\n### Frontend migration comparison tests\n\nThe frontend migration comparison tests validate that backend and frontend conversion logic produce consistent results:\n\n- **Test methodology**: Compares backend vs frontend conversion outputs through DashboardModel integration\n- **Dataset coverage**: Tests run against curated test files covering various conversion scenarios\n- **Test location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts`\n- **Test data**: Located in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/testdata/input/` and `testdata/output/`\n\n**Test execution:**\n```bash\n# Frontend migration comparison tests\nyarn test DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts\n```\n\n**Test approach:**\n- **Frontend path**: `jsonInput → DashboardModel → DashboardMigrator → getSaveModelClone()`\n- **Backend path**: `jsonInput → Backend Conversion → backendOutput → DashboardModel → getSaveModelClone()`\n- **Comparison**: Direct comparison of final converted states from both paths\n\nFor schema version migration testing details, see the [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md).\n\n## Monitoring Migrations\n\nThe dashboard migration system provides comprehensive observability through metrics, logging, and error classification to monitor conversion operations.\n\n### Metrics\n\nThe dashboard migration system now provides comprehensive observability through:\n- **Prometheus metrics** for tracking conversion success/failure rates and performance\n- **Structured logging** for debugging and monitoring conversion operations\n- **Automatic instrumentation** via wrapper functions that eliminate code duplication\n- **Error classification** to distinguish between different types of migration failures\n\n#### 1. Dashboard conversion success metric\n\n**Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total`\n\n**Type:** Counter\n\n**Description:** Total number of successful dashboard conversions\n\n**Labels:**\n- `source_version_api` - Source API version (e.g., \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\")\n- `target_version_api` - Target API version (e.g., \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\")\n- `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (e.g., \"16\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\n- `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (e.g., \"41\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\n\n**Example:**\n```prometheus\ngrafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total{\n  source_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n  target_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n  source_schema_version=\"16\",\n  target_schema_version=\"41\"\n} 1250\n```\n\n#### 2. Dashboard conversion failure metric\n\n**Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total`\n\n**Type:** Counter\n\n**Description:** Total number of failed dashboard conversions\n\n**Labels:**\n- `source_version_api` - Source API version\n- `target_version_api` - Target API version  \n- `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\n- `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\n- `error_type` - Classification of the error (see Error Types section)\n\n**Example:**\n```prometheus\ngrafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total{\n  source_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n  target_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n  source_schema_version=\"14\",\n  target_schema_version=\"41\",\n  error_type=\"schema_version_migration_error\"\n} 42\n```\n\n### Error Types\n\nThe `error_type` label classifies failures into three categories:\n\n#### 1. `conversion_error`\n- General conversion failures not related to schema migration\n- API-level conversion issues\n- Programming errors in conversion functions\n\n#### 2. `schema_version_migration_error`\n- Failures during individual schema version migrations (v14→v15, v15→v16, etc.)\n- Schema-specific transformation errors\n- Data format incompatibilities\n\n#### 3. `schema_minimum_version_error`\n- Dashboards with schema versions below the minimum supported version (< v13)\n- These are logged as warnings rather than errors\n- Indicates dashboards that cannot be migrated automatically\n\n### Logging\n\n#### Log structure\n\nAll migration logs use structured logging with consistent field names:\n\n**Base Fields (always present):**\n- `sourceVersionAPI` - Source API version\n- `targetVersionAPI` - Target API version\n- `dashboardUID` - Unique identifier of the dashboard being converted\n\n**Schema Version Fields (v0/v1 dashboards only):**\n- `sourceSchemaVersion` - Source schema version number\n- `targetSchemaVersion` - Target schema version number\n- `erroredSchemaVersionFunc` - Name of the schema migration function that failed (on error)\n\n**Error Fields (failures only):**\n- `errorType` - Same classification as metrics error_type label\n- `erroredConversionFunc` - Name of the conversion function that failed\n- `error` - The actual error message\n\n#### Log levels\n\n##### Success (DEBUG level)\n```json\n{\n  \"level\": \"debug\",\n  \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion succeeded\",\n  \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n  \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n  \"dashboardUID\": \"abc123\",\n  \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 16,\n  \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41\n}\n```\n\n##### Conversion/Migration Error (ERROR level)\n```json\n{\n  \"level\": \"error\", \n  \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion failed\",\n  \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n  \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n  \"erroredConversionFunc\": \"Convert_V0_to_V1\",\n  \"dashboardUID\": \"abc123\",\n  \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 16,\n  \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41,\n  \"erroredSchemaVersionFunc\": \"V24\",\n  \"errorType\": \"schema_version_migration_error\",\n  \"error\": \"migration failed: table panel plugin not found\"\n}\n```\n\n##### Minimum Version Error (WARN level)\n```json\n{\n  \"level\": \"warn\",\n  \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion failed\", \n  \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n  \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n  \"erroredConversionFunc\": \"Convert_V0_to_V1\",\n  \"dashboardUID\": \"def456\",\n  \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 10,\n  \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41,\n  \"erroredSchemaVersionFunc\": \"\",\n  \"errorType\": \"schema_minimum_version_error\",\n  \"error\": \"dashboard schema version 10 cannot be migrated\"\n}\n```\n\n### Implementation Details\n\n#### Automatic instrumentation\n\nAll dashboard conversions are automatically instrumented via the `withConversionMetrics` wrapper function:\n\n```go\n// All conversion functions are wrapped automatically\ns.AddConversionFunc((*dashv0.Dashboard)(nil), (*dashv1.Dashboard)(nil),\n    withConversionMetrics(dashv0.APIVERSION, dashv1.APIVERSION, func(a, b interface{}, scope conversion.Scope) error {\n        return Convert_V0_to_V1(a.(*dashv0.Dashboard), b.(*dashv1.Dashboard), scope)\n    }))\n```\n\n#### Error handling\n\nCustom error types provide structured error information:\n\n```go\n// Schema migration errors\ntype MigrationError struct {\n    msg            string\n    targetVersion  int\n    currentVersion int\n    functionName   string\n}\n\n// API conversion errors  \ntype ConversionError struct {\n    msg               string\n    functionName      string\n    currentAPIVersion string\n    targetAPIVersion  string\n}\n```\n\n### Registration\n\n#### Metrics registration\n\nMetrics must be registered with Prometheus during service initialization:\n\n```go\nimport \"github.com/grafana/grafana/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration\"\n\n// Register metrics with Prometheus\nmigration.RegisterMetrics(prometheusRegistry)\n```\n\n#### Available metrics\n\nThe following metrics are available after registration:\n\n```go\n// Success counter\nmigration.MDashboardConversionSuccessTotal\n\n// Failure counter  \nmigration.MDashboardConversionFailureTotal\n```\n\n## The README confirms that schema versions range from v13 to v42, and that schema version migrations apply to v0alpha1 and v1beta1 dashboards. Now I have enough information to write the investigation report. Let me compile all my findings:\n\n**Root Cause:**\n- File: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n- Function: `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)\n- Specific issue: Lines 120-123 have an early return condition\n\n**The Bug:**\nThe code returns early if `defaults[\"custom\"]` doesn't exist or isn't a map. This early return occurs BEFORE the `migrateOverrides` function is called at line 135. As a result:\n1. This causes field overrides with `custom.displayMode` to be silently dropped during dashboard import, affecting all dashboards from pre-v10.4 versions that have field overrides without explicit defaults configuration.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n**Function:** `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)\n**Mechanism:** Lines 120-123 perform an early return that prevents execution of the override migration logic\n\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // Early return if custom is not a map\n}\n```\n\nThis early return occurs **before** the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call at line 135, which is the function responsible for migrating field override properties from `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions`.\n\n### The Problematic Control Flow\n\n```\nprocessPanelsV38():\n  ├─ Line 110-113: Validate fieldConfig exists\n  ├─ Line 115-118: Validate defaults exists\n  ├─ Line 120-123: Check for defaults.custom\n  │   └─ ❌ RETURN IF NOT FOUND (breaks control flow)\n  ├─ Line 126-132: Migrate defaults.custom.displayMode\n  └─ Line 135: migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  ← Never reached if custom is missing\n```\n\nWhen `defaults[\"custom\"]` doesn't exist or is not a map, the function continues to the next panel without calling `migrateOverrides`, which leaves field override properties in the legacy `custom.displayMode` format instead of migrating them to the new `custom.cellOptions` structure.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Early Return Condition (v38.go:120-123)\nThe problematic code is clearly visible:\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // This prevents migrateOverrides from being called\n}\n```\n\n### 2. Override Migration Function Placement (v38.go:135)\nThe `migrateOverrides` call is placed **after** the early return check:\n```go\n// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions\nif displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n    // ... process defaults.custom.displayMode\n}\n\n// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // Only called if custom exists\n```\n\n### 3. Override Migration Function Signature (v38.go:140)\nThe `migrateOverrides` function can operate independently from defaults.custom:\n```go\nfunc migrateOverrides(fieldConfig map[string]interface{}) {\n    overrides, ok := fieldConfig[\"overrides\"].([]interface{})\n    // ... processes overrides array directly from fieldConfig\n}\n```\nThis function receives the entire `fieldConfig` object and doesn't require `defaults.custom` to exist. However, it is never invoked when `defaults.custom` is missing.\n\n### 4. Test Coverage Gap\nAll test cases in `v38_test.go` include explicit `custom` fields in defaults (lines 23-29, 36-42, etc.), masking the regression for dashboards without explicit custom configuration.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **Package:** `github.com/grafana/grafana/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion`\n2. **Module:** Dashboard migration pipeline (v0alpha1/v1beta1 to v1beta1)\n3. **Scope:** Table panels in dashboards with schema versions < 38 being migrated to v38\n4. **Impact:** Field overrides configuration for table cell display modes\n\n### Migration Chain\n\n```\nDashboard Import → Migration Pipeline (v13→v42) → V38 (Regression Point)\n                 ↓\n            processPanelsV38()\n                 ↓\n            [Check for defaults.custom]\n                 ↓\n            ❌ Early return if missing\n                 ↓\n            ✗ migrateOverrides() skipped\n                 ↓\n            Field overrides remain unmigrated (legacy format)\n```\n\n## Why Dashboards with Explicit `defaults.custom` Are Unaffected\n\nDashboards that explicitly define `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` satisfy the type assertion at line 120:\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n// custom exists, so execution continues...\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // ✓ This gets called\n```\n\nThese dashboards successfully reach the `migrateOverrides` call, which properly converts field override properties from `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions`.\n\n## Schema Version Trigger\n\n- **Affected Version:** v38\n- **Affects Dashboards:** Imported from any version < 38\n- **Version Released:** As part of Grafana v10.4+ (schema versions 13-42 support v0alpha1/v1beta1 dashboards)\n- **Minimum Supported Version:** v13 (per migration/README.md line 82)\n- **Latest Version:** v42\n\nThe migration executes when:\n1. Dashboard schemaVersion is < 38\n2. Dashboard is being migrated through the schema version pipeline\n3. Dashboard contains table panels with field overrides\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:** Restructure the conditional logic to ensure `migrateOverrides` is called for all table panels regardless of whether `defaults.custom` exists.\n\n**Implementation Approach:**\n1. Move the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call outside of the `defaults.custom` existence check\n2. Ensure it executes whenever fieldConfig and defaults exist, independent of custom field presence\n3. Process `defaults.custom.displayMode` separately (only when custom exists)\n4. Process field overrides independently (always when fieldConfig.overrides exists)\n\n**Test Coverage Addition:**\nAdd test cases covering:\n- Table panels with field overrides but no explicit `defaults.custom`\n- Table panels with overrides referencing `custom.displayMode` where defaults.custom doesn't exist\n- Nested panels with the same missing custom field scenario\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4678,"cache_read_input_tokens":48011,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4678},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3a66ac7c-9cb2-4d33-b608-149632a8e1e6","uuid":"d4a48390-55b8-44b2-9fcf-fb4e199d1d8e"}

The code has an early return condition that **prevents override migration** when a table panel's `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` field is not explicitly set.\n\n### The Problem\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // Returns here, skipping migrateOverrides at line 135\n}\n```\n\nThis early return occurs **before** the `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call that should migrate field overrides from `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions`. As a result:\n\n1. **Dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`** → Field overrides are silently dropped\n2. **Dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom`** → Field overrides are properly migrated (because the code reaches `migrateOverrides`)\n\n### Impact\n- Affects all dashboards from pre-v10.4 versions (schema < 38) with table panels that have field overrides\n- Field overrides with `custom.displayMode` are never converted to the new `custom.cellOptions` format\n- Column formatting configuration is silently lost during dashboard import\n\n### Migration Chain Affected\nDashboard Import → v13→...→v37 → **v38 (Regression Point)** → v39→...→v42\n\nThe detailed report is ready at `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with code references, evidence, and recommendations."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2070,"cache_read_input_tokens":52689,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2070},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3a66ac7c-9cb2-4d33-b608-149632a8e1e6","uuid":"c111a349-d947-4f26-add0-feec5a3c3714"}
